Sighted students, and those with disabilities other than visual impairments, can use Code Jumper too, so everyone can collaborate and work together in one classroom. Code Jumper was developed by Microsoft and is distributed by the American Printing House for the Blind (APH).\r\n    Code Jumper is an easy platform to help students build the skills necessary for a modern workplace. Students will utilize flexibility and computational thinking as they experiment, predict, question, and practice fundamental programming concepts in a very concrete and tangible way. \r\n    Most existing coding tools are highly visual in nature, both in how code is manipulated (such as dragging and dropping coding blocks) and in how the code behaves (such as showing animations). This makes them inaccessible to students who are visually impaired.
